  20. This product is simply the best I've ever owned, and I have had three from the most expensive to the chain-pharmacy-bought cheapest. Its design is genius, though its engineering may be the reason it took a company that actually designed shavers for decades to actually produce this innovation. All other nose trimmers are locked into a tube-shaped design with a spinning circle of blades entrusted with the task of trimming your nose hairs. The problem with that design is that there is nothing holding the hair in place when the blade hits it (as on an electric razor which first captures the hair), so the hair can bend away from the blade. Depending only on speed and sharpness of the blade is the deficiency of an architecture that is hit and miss, and, if you push too hard to \\"help\\" catch the hair, you can cause a pinch of skin. Trying to trim ear hairs with a tube-shape is useless (you can actually hear when it cuts hair, which is rare). Eyebrows are not even on the menu. Norelco has simply reproduced a miniature--no, make that micro-shaver and placed it on the side of the thin, slanted tube. I have never trimmed my nose hairs with such efficiency and comfort. Ear hairs are also amazingly cut on the first pass. And the attachment for eyebrows makes the results as good--and as simple--as when my barber does it for me. I immediately bought two more for family members. Two year warranty. All literature indicates it's made in the USA.

  142. [April 27th, 2011 update: My final unit has lasted more than a year now and I have therefore added a star to the rating. The dying problem, as some other reviews have pointed out, is actually a \\"sticking\\" problem. When the blades get some mucus moisture on them, they will stick after it dries out. So, when you go to turn the unit on in a day or two, the unit appears dead. There are two possible fixes: 1) Disassemble and clean the head assembly. 2) Gently tap the side of the head assembly against a counter until it works. I have used #2 successfully on many occasions. Had I tried that approach on the previous units I purchased, I'm sure they would have all worked. Still, I would call this a design flaw (see below) because it sticks so easily and so often. [July 12th, 2009 update: My fourth one just died. I think they fail when they get just a bit of moisture on the blades. I've contacted Norelco customer support but they don't seem concerned. Meanwhile, the competition is figuring out that this design is pretty decent. There are other choices, like the Remington MPT-3000 Precision Trimmer]. I think this is the best nose hair trimmer design I've ever used, and I've used several different types (rotary style, spatula style, scissors, etc). However, I've had two of these Norelco's fail on me within three weeks of usage. The last one lasted 2 months before dying. Fortunately, I'm buying them at the local Fry's, so I just keep taking them back and getting a new one (sorry folks, but I'd actually recommend, in this case, that you buy them locally at a place with a decent return policy). I'm not sure if there's just a bad batch or if there's a pathological design flaw. I'm on my fourth one (fingers crossed). When it fails, it just stops working, and I just use it occasionally for light nose trimming. I never use the accessories or travel with it. I wish a Norelco rep would step-up and deal with this. I give it four stars for design and nose trimming, and one star for quality control. Final rating: 3 stars.

  332. I had the original MicroTouch razor for over five years before it eventually it broke down. I was looking at the new(er) MicroTouch razor but it still looked a bit cheap. So I decided to look for a better replacement.<br /><br />The Norelco is essentially the MicroTouch but with a much better design and feel to it. The on/off rotating switch works flawlessly and is quite smooth. The NT9110 is quite the upgrade. The quality of parts is impressive and even the attachments fit perfectly (which didn't really happen with the MicroTouch.)<br /><br />Likely for safety requirements, Norelco enhanced the blade by making it smaller and flush with the head of the trimmer body. This enhancement adds improved looks and gives it a professional appearance.<br /><br />My only minor complaint is that by enhancing the trimmer's appearance Norelco sacrifices a bit of performance from the blade. By having a slightly taller blade, the MicroTouch was very effective at removing hair. It had this gentle \\"scrape\\" quality that took getting use to -- but was not uncomfortable or painful in any way. The Norelco prevents this \\"scrape\\" ability since the blade is flush to the body; however, the trimming action is less effective. Fortunatley, this change just requires a bit more pressure and force to remove those stubborn hairs. Due to this change, I probably take twice as long than before -- a significant difference but not critical.<br /><br />The sleek design offers a thicker, rubber grip which allows for positive control even when using wet. The battery compartment is well-engineered into the on/off switch. The unit just requires (1) AA battery -- unlike the MicroTouch's (2) AAA batteries -- which are usually more expensive.<br /><br />At first glance, a rechargeable battery system with a little docking station would have been cute but the alkaline battery system makes it better for travel and less prone to charging failures. Obviously, it saves on consumer cost too.<br /><br />I'm confident that this Norelco will last a long time. The unit is water-resistant (within reason) and is very easy to clean with a splash of water.

  337. My first trimmer was a Panasonic ER411NC. It was a very good trimmer, providing me with an elegant solution to a problem that most men start to have once they reach middle age: nasal hair. The Panasonic has a circular tip that has small, slit-like openings. Inside the tip is a spinning blade. The hair gets caught between the slits and the spinning blade. That is how it cuts. I wrote a review of that trimmer back in July of 2004 and gave it 4 stars.<br /><br />My second trimmer was another Panasonic, ER421KC. This one had a small LED light to help you see while trimming under your nose. I bought it to replace the ER411NC after it fell off the counter and damaged its blades. The ER421NC is very uncomfortable. Althought it uses the same blade design as the ER411NC, the motor seems to be weaker. It is easily stopped. The spinning blade sometimes cannot cut the hair that gets caught between the slits and itself. The hair can force the blades to stop spinning. It will be hard to remove without pulling the hair out. This is very uncomfortable, to say the least. It will bring tears to your eyes.<br /><br />I bought this Norelco (the subject of this review) to replace the second Panasonic. The design of the Norelco is different. It cannot be forced to stop by your hair. It uses the same cutting design as your sideburn and mustache trimmer. So far, it has proven itself to be comfortable. However, it does take longer and more effort to trim with the Norelco. You will have to make sure that the hairs that you want to trim are caught between the oscillating blades of the trimmer. And, since the blades are small, this could take a few minutes of your time. Whereas with the Panasonic, all you need do is stick the tip in your nose and move it from side to side. With the Norelco, you will have to be more deliberate. However, it is the most comfortable of the three. Plus, you can use the Norelco to trim your eyebrows, if you need that sort of thing. It is also the easiest to clean out of the three.<br /><br />I believe this will be a good trimmer for you, if you value comfort above any other consideration. This trimmer is waterproof and it can be washed with warm water.est to clean out of the three. I believe this will be a good trimmer for you, if you value comfort above any other consideration. This trimmer is waterproof and it can be washed with warm water.

Likewise, the Mangroomer was only used 1 more time and now sits in a toiletry bag. I have no idea if it still works or not, and have no desire to ever try it again.<br /><br />Now that I've had the Philips Norelco NT9110 for about 2 years, and recently remembered my prior reviews, I decided to update it. This is by far the better of the 4 trimmers. I read back then about other people having problems with water or rust, or something like that, so I always made sure to blow any access water out after cleaning it. I also never put the cap back on. Instead, I stored it in an open place where the blades wouldn't get damaged, and any moisture left behind would still be able to dissipate. I've never had a problem.<br /><br />I had noticed this trimmer before, but something about the design turned me away from buying it. For whatever reason, I felt the other rotary designs would/should be superior, but they're not. The Philips Norelco cuts just as close as any of other trimmers, it has never pulled one hair, and its never cut me (which was a concern with this design, and I've jammed/pushed it into any areas as needed). If you put the plastic protective cap on as is, it will NEVER dry and will corrode the works inside. To alleviate this, I put several holes through the cap. To do this, heat an ice pick or awl and poke away. I suppose a Dremel-like tool could cut holes or slots as well and may be safer. In any case, make sure there is plenty of ventilation so that the device will dry thoroughly or leave the cover off until it is COMPLETELY dry.<br /><br />2) It's too loud to use for the hair in my ears. If you twist too far, the barrel comes apart in your hands revealing the battery.   565. This is a great tool, really handy and effective... it just has one major problem.. It suddenly stops working!! And do not think as I did that this will not happen to you as it happened to other reviewers, most probable it will suddenly stop without a clear reason.<br /><br />I fixed mine by myself, it still stop working from time to time, now I know how to fix it.<br /><br />It seems to be a design problem, and what makes it stop working is mechanism lock (just beneath the blades. Unfortunately you will not be able to reach that mechanism without removing the small decorative plastic around the blades(you will need something sharp and fine to do so. Then you will need a needle just to give couple of strokes up and down to a small white plastic thing just beneath the blades... you may need some force to do so, do not worry. This will unlock the mechanism and make it work again.<br /><br />So, for those not technical or who will be little bit lazy to do that, I suggest hitting the unit (vertically) while it is ON against something semi-hard, this may unlock the mechanism.<br /><br />Hope this will work for you as it did for me, otherwise maybe it will be better to return it and get a different model<br /><br />I definitely would rate it 4 or 5 stars if it was durable.<br /><br />Regards,<br /><br />Karamany

  575. [[VIDEOID:moAZ8ZO299X85H]]Let's be honest, reviewing a nose/ear/eyebrow hair trimmer is not the most pleasant task in the world, nor is watching a video review of same. So I will make it a bit easier by not actually demonstrating the use of it. You'll thank me later for that :-)<br /><br />In my video I will merely describe how it works. So in that regard it's G-rated and fun for the entire family to watch.<br /><br />I've used scissors, rotary trimmers, and on occasion have grabbed unruly nose hairs to remove them from unattractive places on my face. And let's face it, any nose hair that is not actually in your nose, is in an unattractive place on your face. Fortunately I don't have ear hair, at least not any that is significantly visible, but If I did, the same argument would apply to those pesky hairs.<br /><br />What I've found with scissors is that they can be dangerous to use in such sensitive places and don't get as close as you might want. Rotary trimmers have typically been quite a painful experience for me. They tend to grab and rip as opposed to smoothly cut, and that can result in a painful experience as well.<br /><br />The Norelco NT9110 trimmer seems to be effective without the grabbing and ripping.<br /><br />The eyebrow attachments come in two sizes, short and long. You're supposed to comb against the grain, that is from the direction of your ear to your nose, when trimming your eyebrows. I had no luck with that. It did not trim, cut or do anything to my eyebrows. Maybe that's good, I'm not sure. But I suspect it's because it works better on hair that is more on the \\"fine\\" side rather than more coarse hair. If my theory is correct, it might work for you better than it worked on my eyebrows.<br /><br />I didn't really buy this with any expectation of trimming my eyebrows though, or ears, only nose. And for that it works great.<br /><br />I don't have a world of experience with nose/ear/eyebrow trimmers, but compared to the two previous rotary trimmers I've used, this is easier to clean, not as painful to use and seems a reasonably priced and mostly effective way to keep those nose hairs in tip-top shape. It's also relatively comfortable to hold and the angled head make it easy to maneuver in and out of those tight places, like noses and ears. I withhold 5 stars simply because it didn't work on my eyebrows but it may for you.<br /><br />Since a number of people have complained about this trimmer not working after just a few uses it's important to remember to clean the trimmer after each use and sometimes even during each use. You need to run warm water over the cutting surface, alternately switching the unit on and off once or twice to dislodge any tiny hair particles. Then air dry and use the brush to finish the cleaning process. This should keep your trimmer happily buzzing along for many exciting nose trimming sessions.<br /><br />Happy trimming!a reasonably priced and mostly effective way to keep those nose hairs in tip-top shape. It's also relatively comfortable to hold and the angled head make it easy to maneuver in and out of those tight places, like noses and ears. I withhold 5 stars simply because it didn't work on my eyebrows but it may for you. Since a number of people have complained about this trimmer not working after just a few uses it's important to remember to clean the trimmer after each use and sometimes even during each use. You need to run warm water over the cutting surface, alternately switching the unit on and off once or twice to dislodge any tiny hair particles. Then air dry and use the brush to finish the cleaning process. This should keep your trimmer happily buzzing along for many exciting nose trimming sessions. Happy trimming!

  625. I don't know of anyone who enjoys trimming the hair in their ears and nose. The task is made more daunting by a market full of underpowered, barely useful powered trimmers. Over the years I have purchased many battery powered nose and ear hair trimmers, most of which end up in the garbage within a year or less. I have tried trimmers from Remington, Conair, Wahl and Panasonic. One had a light and one even had a vacuum, and most of them were wet/dry devices that would be rinsed out with water. All seemed like a good purchase at the time but all of them had the same problem: NOT ENOUGH POWER.<br /><br />Considering that most of these small trimmers are powered by a single AA battery, the lack of power only makes sense. After all, a single AA battery only provides 1.5 volts of power. Another annoying problem is that most of these devices would not maintain a consistent blade speed. I would find that when first turned on the units would sound fine but as soon as I started to cut the motor would start slowing way down and would begin fluctuating between faster and slower speeds. Of course slower blade speed leads to the potential of hairs getting caught, causing the discomfort of pulling. I can honestly tell you that having your nose hairs pulled is extremely unpleasant. Even though it rarely made a difference, I regularly installed new batteries in hopes that the trimmers would provide more power and fast enough blade speed to prevent pulling the hairs in my nose and ears. Eventually I just gave up and threw the device away and would buy a different model.<br /><br />Recently I decided to give the Philips Norelco NT9110 Precision Nose and Ear Trimmer a try. The patented tube shave technology promises \\"no pulling and prevents nicks and cuts.\\" I also liked the looks of the angled head, which claims to give better reach and control. The Norelco NT9110 also doubles as an eyebrow trimmer, which was also an intriguing feature to me. The cost of this trimmer on Amazon is very low so I decided to give it a try.<br /><br />I received my order within a couple of days and eagerly tore into the packaging to retrieve my new trimmer. Of course in was incased in one of those clamshell cases, which took me no less than 5 minutes to cut and tear open. I HATE those clamshell cases and wish manufacturers would develop a new way of packaging their products! Anyway, I installed the included AA battery and switched the trimmer on. It came to life with a soft hum and I began the task of mowing the hair in my ears and nose. The blade speed remained consistent and there was no pulling discomfort at all. Cleaning the blade under running water is an effortless task. I then placed one of the eyebrow combs on the blade-head and trimmed my eyebrows, which provided satisfactory results.<br /><br />I have been using this Norelco trimmer now for a couple of weeks and couldn't be happier with my purchase. The NT9110 gives a close cut, provides adequate power and consistent blade speed, and causes no discomfort whatsoever. I also find that the angled tube shaped cutter head is easy to maneuver and doesn't cause as much of a tickling sensation in the nose as the typical rotary trimmers do. This is by far the best nose and ear hair trimmer that I have used and I hope it continues to provide great service for many months or years to come. I am concerned because several other reviewers have stated that their Norelco NT9110 died after only a few weeks of use. I feel that it is extremely important that the owner cleans the device after each use, as the tube shaped cutter is small, and trapped hairs in the cutter assembly could easily cause the blade system to jam. I also recommend placing a drop of blade oil (not included with this trimmer) on the cutter assembly every now and then, to keep it properly lubricated. I think that any moving parts, when rinsed in water, should be lubricated with a light oil to keep the parts moving freely. However, Norelco does not require this or even suggest it in the owner's manual. It is just my personal suggestion. So far I am extremely pleased with the Philips Norelco NT9110 Precision Nose and Ear Trimmer and would highly recommend it to all men looking for a powerful, battery operated trimmer. I will provide an update to this review if my trimmer fails or begins working with less satisfying results in the future.ire this or even suggest it in the owner's manual. I try to keep it clean, which means running the blade head through some faucet water after I am done using it and then leaving it out to dry.<br /><br />As far as I can tell the blade head is not meant to be removable, which (unfortunately) makes this a disposable product. I would prefer to be able to replace the blade head if/when necessary. Like with the battery, which surprisingly can last for many months of use(in my experience). The method of operation is very simple - just align the blades in a manner where the front(cutting edge) of the blades will befacing the hairs you intend to cut, move it across the face at a slight angle parallel to the skin. I likely will buy another one again in the future to replace this one.

And we've thrown away the earlier trimmers. I highly recommend this product. ------- UPDATE 03-21-2009: Wow. By many of the reviews here, it's easy to see that people just return or toss something that stops working. How about reading the instructions? This trimmer is excellent, when used properly. I rinse mine in hot water for a few seconds with each use, shake it, quickly pat it with a towel and put the cap back on. It never fails. My wife has one as well. She rarely rinses. Soon, her trimmer fails. She's ready to throw it away. Instead, to prove my point, I poured a half inch of kitchen vinegar into a small Dixie cup, set the dead trimmer to \\"on\\", immersed it into the vinegar and swirled it around. In THREE SECONDS, the trimmer came back from the dead. Before you say this is a design flaw, take a look at Braun's premium face shavers for men. They now come with a replaceable fluid cleaner reservoir. After EVERY use, the shaver is returned to its pedestal, where you, the customer, are entrusted to push a button to begin the daily cleaning process. If you do, the shaver works perfectly every time. With the Philips trimmer, you also need to do a tiny bit of maintenance to keep it running. Douse it under hot water, shake off the water, put on itscap. And make sure it doesn't have a dead battery. If you can't do that, don't blame Philips. Or Amazon. Just buy a non-electric pair of tiny scissors and enjoy.

  920. Among a selection of pocket-sized trimmers, this one truly stands out in quality and elegant design. Similar to the other reticulated (angled backward) trimmer designs, but without the gaudy neon-glow colors. A simple twist-to-activate design eliminates any battery-or-switch confusion; just be careful not to twist too far and expose the battery when turning it off. Unlike the more compact competitors, this one uses a double-A battery, rather than a tiny triple-A battery. This means longer battery life, more consistent power and less jamming. Leave the AAA batteries for your remote. Another great thing about the Philips model is a smooth, rounded design to the tip; comfortable and gentle on sensitive areas, like the nostril and the ear. The trimmer combs are recessed from the tip, meaning you won't get a nasty surprise while turning it inside those same sensitive areas. A bit more cost, but it is definitely worth it.
  921. Bought this thing nearly 5 years ago (on 6/25/2008) and it is still doing its job regularly. When I read the reviews back then, I did note a lot of people saying it would inexplicably go dead on them. However, having owned and operated my share of cheapo flashlights and other electronics over the years, I had an idea that I knew what was causing it (i.e. not the motor going dead) and how to fix it.<br /><br />Sure enough, after about a month, mine went dead as well. Now, if you pull it apart (like you are changing the battery) and take a good look at how the steel tabs are supposed to make contact when you twist it to turn it on, it is pretty easy to - gently - bend them a little bit with something like a small eyeglass screwdriver so they make more solid contact. A minor tweak or two and viola, mine has ran like a champ for nearly five years and still going (knock on wood). Judging by some of the recent one-star reviews, it would appear that Norelco hasn't exactly bothered to fix the problem. So if you buy one, just expect you might have to tweak the contacts a little bit - absolutely no biggie.<br /><br />As for how well it works as a nose trimmer, I have to say that it felt really weird the first few times I used it and wasn't really sure it was going to work out, but eventually got used to it and now can't imagine anything working better. I use it once a week. Immediately after use (and while it is still turned on), I run the blades under a stream of warm water, then turn it off and, like that other bathroom ritual, give it a couple of shakes and put it away. Can't remember changing the battery more than twice in the last five years - but when I have changed it, it was like a whole new machine, so should probably change it a little more often. I'm guessing every year or so would be a good time to change the battery for weekly use.<br /><br />Whenever this one finally quits working, will definitely buy another one - and I would recommend it to anyone who is not afraid of possibly having to tweak the contact tabs a little to get it working properly at some point.

I've never had to use it as an ear trimmer because I don't really have ear hair but I'm sure the performance is similar to it's nose hair capabilities.<br /><br />My primary use though is the eyebrow trimmer. I know most guys might not care about this but I'm not ashamed to say I have bushy eyebrows that need some tending every once in a while and this is the perfect tool for the job. It trims them down to two different sizes with the two included comb attachments and is also good for trimming any stray hairs around the eyebrows. I also use it to pick up any strays I might miss while shaving and any other stray hairs I find poking out. It's a soft, vibrating blade that causes no irritation and has really exceptional battery life for something powered by a conventional battery. Cleanup is also very simple.<br /><br />Obviously this isn't going to be the answer for everyone. The attachments are small and easy to misplace but the body of the unit itself seems very sturdy for being made of plastic. Like I said, my original one is still going strong even after three years. If you need a simple nose and ear trimmer or if you're particular about your eyebrows like me, you can't beat this product for the price.

The only logical conclusion I could come to is that Norelco had quality control issues during that era.<br /><br />Yet it is now 2013 and I can attest to the superior cutting mechanism Norelco uses.
